<script>
  function getColors(color) {
    let lightColor = tinycolor(color);
    let darkColor = tinycolor(color);
    const lightBrightness = lightColor.getBrightness();
    if (lightBrightness <= 80)
      lightColor.lighten(50);
    else if (80 < lightBrightness && lightBrightness <= 190)
      lightColor.lighten(20);
    return {
      light: lightBrightness > 190 ? color : lightColor.toString(),
      dark: darkColor.darken().toString(),
    }
  }
  function toggleDropdown(dropdownId) {
    dropdown = document.getElementById(dropdownId);
    if (dropdown) {
      if (dropdown.style.display == "flex") dropdown.style.display = "none";
      else {
        document.querySelectorAll('#main-header .hsp-dropdown').forEach(dropdown => dropdown.style.display = 'none');
        dropdown.style.display = "flex";
      }
    }
  }
  function toggleText(textId) {
    const element = document.getElementById(textId);
    if (element.style.display == 'block') {
      element.style.overflowY = 'hidden';
      element.style.display = '-webkit-box';
    }
    else {
      element.style.overflowY = "unset";
      element.style.display = "block";
    }
  }
  function openPopupWelcome() {
    document.getElementById("popup-overlay").style.display = 'block';
  }
  function closePopupWelcome() {
    document.getElementById("popup-overlay").style.display = 'none';
  }
  async function subscribe() {
    const response = await fetch('/public/subscribe/lex-fridman-podcast-artificial-intelligence-ai', {
      method: 'PUT',
      headers: {
        'Content-Type': 'text/plain',
        'X-CSRF-TOKEN': document.querySelector('meta[name="csrf-token"]').content
      },
    });
    if (response.ok) {
      let subscribeBtn = document.getElementById('btn-subscribe');
      subscribeBtn.classList.add("hsp-btn-active", "pseudo-check");
      subscribeBtn.classList.remove("hsp-btn-ready");
      subscribeBtn.textContent = "SUBSCRIBED";
      subscribeBtn.onclick = unsubscribe;

      const subscriberCount = document.getElementById('subscriber-count');
      const newCount = parseInt(subscriberCount.textContent.split()[0], 10) + 1;
      subscriberCount.textContent = newCount.toString() + (newCount == 1 ? " subscriber" : " subscribers");
    }
  }
  async function unsubscribe() {
    const response = await fetch('/public/unsubscribe/lex-fridman-podcast-artificial-intelligence-ai', {
      method: 'PUT',
      headers: {
        'Content-Type': 'text/plain',
        'X-CSRF-TOKEN': document.querySelector('meta[name="csrf-token"]').content
      },
    });
    if (response.ok) {
      let subscribeBtn = document.getElementById('btn-subscribe');
      subscribeBtn.classList.add("hsp-btn-ready");
      subscribeBtn.classList.remove("hsp-btn-active", "pseudo-check");
      subscribeBtn.textContent = "SUBSCRIBE";
      subscribeBtn.onclick = subscribe;

      const subscriberCount = document.getElementById('subscriber-count');
      const newCount = parseInt(subscriberCount.textContent.split()[0], 10) - 1;
      subscriberCount.textContent = newCount.toString() + (newCount == 1 ? " subscriber" : " subscribers");
    }
  }
  function signUp() {
    window.location.href = '/users/sign_up?next=' + window.location.href;
  }

    <p class="hsp-card-podcast-description" title="Description">Utopia or dystopia? It’s up to us.
In the 21st century, powerful technologies have been appearing at a breathtaking pace—related to the internet, artificial intelligence, genetic engineering, and more. They have amazing potential upsides, but we can’t ignore the serious risks that come with them.
Brave New Planet is a podcast that delves deep into the most exciting and challenging scientific frontiers, helping us understand them and grapple with their implications. Dr. Eric Lander, president and founding director of the Broad Institute of MIT and Harvard, is a geneticist, molecular biologist, and mathematician who was a leader of the Human Genome Project and for eight years served as a science advisor to the White House for President Obama. He’s also the host of Brave New Planet, and he’s talked to leading researchers, journalists, doctors, policy makers, activists, and legal experts to illuminate how this generation’s choices will shape the future as never before.
Brave New Planet is a partnership between the Broad Institute, Pushkin Industries, and The Boston Globe's Opinion team.</p>

    <h3 class="hsp-card-episode-title" title="Episode Name">#111 – Richard Karp: Algorithms and Computational Complexity</h3>
    <h4 class="hsp-card-episode-podcast-title" title="Podcast Name">Lex Fridman Podcast</h4>
    <ul class="hsp-card-episode-stats" title="Statistics">
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat view-count" title="View Count">220 views</li>
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat date" title="Upload Date">5 months ago</li>
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat duration" title="Duration">02:08:00</li>
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat progress" title="Progress" id="progress-c20b3e98580248c4a026b51ea653126c"></li>
    </ul>
      <p class="hsp-card-episode-description" title="Description">Richard Karp is a professor at Berkeley and one of the most important figures in the history of theoretical computer science. In 1985, he received the Turing Award for his research in the theory of algorithms, including the development of the Edmonds–Karp algorithm for solving the maximum flow problem on networks, Hopcroft–Karp algorithm for finding maximum cardinality matchings in bipartite graphs, and his landmark paper in complexity theory called “Reducibility Among Combinatorial Problems”, in which he proved 21 problems to be NP-complete. This paper was probably the most important catalyst in the explosion of interest in the study of NP-completeness</p>
  </div>
</a>

      <p class="hsp-card-episode-description" title="Description">Peter Singer is a professor of bioethics at Princeton, best known for his 1975 book Animal Liberation, that makes an ethical case against eating meat. He was a key popularizer of the effective altruism movement and is generally considered one of the most influential philosophers in the world.     <h4 class="hsp-card-episode-podcast-title" title="Podcast Name">Lex Fridman Podcast</h4>
    <ul class="hsp-card-episode-stats" title="Statistics">

      <p class="hsp-card-episode-description" title="Description">William MacAskill is a philosopher, ethicist, and one of the originators of the effective altruism movement. His research focuses on the fundamentals of effective altruism – the use of evidence and reason to help others by as much as possible with our time and money, with a particular concentration on how to act given moral uncertainty. He is the author of Doing Good Better – Effective Altruism and a Radical New Way to Make a Difference. He is a co-founder and the President of the Centre for Effective Altruism (CEA) that encourages people to commit to donate at least 10%</p>

His work has been cited over 200,000 times.   <div class="hsp-card-episode-info" title="Information">
    <h3 class="hsp-card-episode-title" title="Episode Name">Daniel Kahneman: Thinking Fast and Slow, Deep Learning, and AI</h3>
    <h4 class="hsp-card-episode-podcast-title" title="Podcast Name">Lex Fridman Podcast</h4>
    <ul class="hsp-card-episode-stats" title="Statistics">
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat view-count" title="View Count">130 views</li>
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat date" title="Upload Date">11 months ago</li>
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat duration" title="Duration">01:19:09</li>
      <li class="hsp-card-episode-stat progress" title="Progress" id="progress-c68d1763f8064b758223783d9887219d"></li>
    </ul>
      <p class="hsp-card-episode-description" title="Description">Daniel Kahneman is winner of the Nobel Prize in economics for his integration of economic science with the psychology of human behavior, judgment and decision-making. He is the author of the popular book “Thinking, Fast and Slow” that summarizes in an accessible way his research of several decades, often in collaboration with Amos Tversky, on cognitive biases, prospect theory, and happiness. The central thesis of this work is a dichotomy between two modes of thought: “System 1” is fast, instinctive and emotional; “System 2” is slower, more deliberative, and more logical. The book delineates cognitive biases associated with each type</p>
  </div>
</a>

      <p class="hsp-card-episode-description" title="Description">Donald Knuth is one of the greatest and most impactful computer scientists and mathematicians ever. He is the recipient in 1974 of the Turing Award, considered the Nobel Prize of computing. He is the author of the multi-volume work, the magnum opus, The Art of Computer Programming. He made several key contributions to the rigorous analysis of the computational complexity of algorithms. He popularized asymptotic notation, that we all affectionately know as the big-O notation. <script>
  $(document).ready(function() {
    const color = "#3A4C50";
    const colors = getColors(color);
    document.querySelector('#main-header').style.background = color;
    document.querySelector('#banner').style.background = 'linear-gradient(0deg,' + colors.dark + ' 0%,' + color + ' 100%)';
    document.querySelector('#header').style.background = 'linear-gradient(0deg, rgba(255,255,255,1) 60%,' + color + ' 100%)';
    document.querySelector('#contributors h2').style.backgroundColor = color;

    const description = document.getElementById("description");
    if (description != null && description.clientHeight != description.scrollHeight) {
      const btnShowDescription = document.getElementById("btn-show-description");
      btnShowDescription.style.display = "block";
      btnShowDescription.addEventListener("click", function() {
        toggleText("description");
        if (btnShowDescription.className == "hsp-btn-toggle more")
          btnShowDescription.className = "hsp-btn-toggle less";
        else btnShowDescription.className = "hsp-btn-toggle more";
      })
    }
  })
</script>
